    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer3307367978773420154"><b>Internationally bestselling author Cecelia Ahern delivers her biggest and most compelling book yet—a tale of secrets, second chances, and the hidden connections that unite our lives</b><br/><br/>Scandal has derailed journalist Kitty Logan's career, a setback that is soon compounded by an even more devastating loss. Constance, the woman who taught Kitty everything she knew, is dying. At </span>
  <span id="freeText3307367978773420154" style="display:none"><b>Internationally bestselling author Cecelia Ahern delivers her biggest and most compelling book yet—a tale of secrets, second chances, and the hidden connections that unite our lives</b><br /><br />Scandal has derailed journalist Kitty Logan's career, a setback that is soon compounded by an even more devastating loss. Constance, the woman who taught Kitty everything she knew, is dying. At her mentor's bedside, Kitty asks her, "What is the one story you always wanted to write?"<br /><br />The answer lies in a single sheet of paper buried in Constance's office—a list of one hundred names—with no notes or explanation. But before Kitty can ask her friend, it is too late.<br /><br />Determined to unlock the mystery and rebuild her own shaky confidence, Kitty throws herself into the investigation, tracking down each of the names on the list and uncovering their connection. Meeting these ordinary people and learning their stories, Kitty begins to piece together an unexpected portrait of Constance's life... and starts to understand her own.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_442956067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/442956067" />
    <a title="Monika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1250052-monika"><img alt="Monika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1213814070p2/1250052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442956067?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monika" href="/user/show/1250052-monika">Monika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250052-monika?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442956067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6946567848763824464">Cecelia Ahern is that rare author that still actually believes in the goodness of people. Maybe it's her youth, maybe she's just that person, but it is so clear that she believes that people are good, that people are beautiful, and that what is most beautiful about life is the story that each of us has to share.<br/><br/>On the surface, you could probably write this off as a sappy chick-lit piece, but it's so much more. You could just read the book and move on, or you could stop and take notice. You might</span>
  <span id="freeText6946567848763824464" style="display:none">Cecelia Ahern is that rare author that still actually believes in the goodness of people. Maybe it's her youth, maybe she's just that person, but it is so clear that she believes that people are good, that people are beautiful, and that what is most beautiful about life is the story that each of us has to share.<br /><br />On the surface, you could probably write this off as a sappy chick-lit piece, but it's so much more. You could just read the book and move on, or you could stop and take notice. You might find yourself smiling as you turn the page, or notice someone else watching the look of warmth on your face while you're reading out in public. You might just find yourself interested in the people around you - the people who pass you on the street, stand in line with you at the cafe, or sit next to you on the bus. If you let it, this story - stories, really - will open you up to all of the interesting things you encounter every day.<br /><br />Stop being cynical, critical, impatient - let Ahern do what she does best. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6946567848763824464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_430622158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430622158" />
    <a title="Megan Readinginthesunshine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11829532-megan-readinginthesunshine"><img alt="Megan Readinginthesunshine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396533386p2/11829532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430622158?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Readinginthesunshine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Readinginthesunshine" href="/user/show/11829532-megan-readinginthesunshine">Megan Readinginthesunshine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430622158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1201888386706401121">I’ve been a big big fan of Cecelia Ahern since I picked up If You Could See Me Now and A Place Called Here many years ago when Cecelia wasn’t as well known as she is now. Something just drew me to the books and I’m so pleased I went with my instinct and bought them because they introduced me to magic in novels, they lifted me up and made me fall in love with books even more. I have since followed Cecelia and bought and loved every single one of her books, so when One Hundred Names was announced </span>
  <span id="freeText1201888386706401121" style="display:none">I’ve been a big big fan of Cecelia Ahern since I picked up If You Could See Me Now and A Place Called Here many years ago when Cecelia wasn’t as well known as she is now. Something just drew me to the books and I’m so pleased I went with my instinct and bought them because they introduced me to magic in novels, they lifted me up and made me fall in love with books even more. I have since followed Cecelia and bought and loved every single one of her books, so when One Hundred Names was announced for release months and months ago, I was filled with that excitement again. And when the book came through my letterbox, I think I jumped around with glee and a massive grin on my face.<br /> <br />I could not wait to start on One Hundred Names, and I was not disappointed. Kitty Logan once had everything going for her, she was a journalist who lived with her boyfriend and she had a great friend in Constance. After Kitty receives false information and confidently but wrongly accuses a man of terrible things, her career is ruined. Colleagues do not want to be associated with her, advertisers are distancing themselves, and Kitty is devastated. As if that wasn’t enough, her boyfriend ups and leaves one day without even telling her. A sad Kitty visits her terminally ill friend Constance in hospital and asks her a thought provoking question: “What is the story you always wanted to write?” Constance directs her to search her office, in which Kitty finds an envelope containing a list of One hundred Names. Sadly, Constance passes away, and with nothing concrete to go on but a list, Kitty sets out to create the perfect tribute to her dear friend – by writing the story Constance never had the opportunity to do.<br /> <br />This story was AMAZING. As with all of Cecelia’s other books I was instantly hooked by her ability to bring the reader into the story and keep them turning the pages. The idea of the story was BEAUTIFUL, truly truly magical. At first I was unsure about how it would pan out, how could Cecelia write a book with one hundred different people’s stories in? How could she even do a few of them without it getting overcrowded? Where would she go with this? But after the first few pages I stopped worrying about all of this and trusted Cecelia had it all planned out, and that turned out to be an understatement, because it was wonderful.<br /> <br />As I said, I very much enjoyed the concept of the story. I enjoyed meeting the new characters and delving into a bit of their life story, hearing and reading about the amazing things that had happened to them, and some of the bravery and courage they have shown. Every story was special, I almost wish there had been more of each!<br /> <br />The characters were intricately and delicately written, each had a very important and special role in the story, and all these pieces put together created something that was truly breathtaking. Kitty was an instantly likeable character, I really felt for her and I found myself backing her all the way, wanting to reach out and hug here when life was not going as planned, and physically cheering in delight at key moments in the story. I think my favourite out of the hundred names were Birdie and Mary-Rose. I loved Birdie’s personality, her positivity, her courage and her determination, I felt she really brought the story alive and her character shone from the pages. Mary-Rose, I liked her story at the beginning and I laughed out loud at the situations she finds herself in. As I read on I liked Mary-Rose not just for what happens in her life, but what she gives to other people, how she always cares for others and has dedicated her life to the happiness of everyone else around her. The other characters also have great parts, but to me, Birdie and Mary-Rose were outstanding.<br /> <br />I won’t spoil the story but I will say that Cecelia is on top form with this one, and has yet again created a world we can delve into for many hours where everything is magical and enthralling, and where you find out that it’s the little things that matter the most. One Hundred Names is compelling, it’s captivating and it’s a beautiful story with an even more precious message. Treasure this book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1201888386706401121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1059727660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1059727660" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1059727660?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007350469" href="/book/show/15732422-one-hundred-names">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=feelgood-wholesome">feelgood-wholesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=chicklit">chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=wishlist-paperback">wishlist-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1059727660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8767459172370355624">There is a reason why Cecelia Ahern is one of my favourite chicklit authors, or simply one of my favourite authors, period. <i>One Hundred Names</i> just confirms that notion and adds a golden star to it. While I don't like all her books, she writes stories with so much spirit, so much love, and with just a dash of humour and magic, and they manage to capture my heart time and time again.<br/><br/><i>One Hundred Names</i> tells the story of Katherine 'Kitty' Logan, who has been blacklisted as a journalist after she mis</span>
  <span id="freeText8767459172370355624" style="display:none">There is a reason why Cecelia Ahern is one of my favourite chicklit authors, or simply one of my favourite authors, period. <i>One Hundred Names</i> just confirms that notion and adds a golden star to it. While I don't like all her books, she writes stories with so much spirit, so much love, and with just a dash of humour and magic, and they manage to capture my heart time and time again.<br /><br /><i>One Hundred Names</i> tells the story of Katherine 'Kitty' Logan, who has been blacklisted as a journalist after she mistakenly scandalised a school teacher. Now her name as a writer is tarnished and no one takes her seriously or wants to work with her. On top of that, her best friend and editor-in-chief Constance just died of cancer. All that Constance has left her is a list of 100 names, and the promise that each of these people has a story to tell. Although these people are quite lovely, they are also quite ordinary and seem to have absolutely nothing in common, nor is there anything juicy to write about. Slowly but surely, though, Kitty manages to find something special in each and every one of the people she meets. She also finally finds her story, and it's one that will warm the coldest cockles of your heart.<br /><br />This is one of the cutest and most charming stories I've ever read. I loved Constance's idea - interviewing a random set of people who may not seem very interesting at first sight, but in the end, everyone's got a story to tell. I'm not actually sure about that; if someone were to call me up for a story right now, I'm sure I'd leave them disappointed, but I love the idea. It's endearing, and Ms Ahern did a wonderful job with portraying so many "normal" people, yet each with their own distinct personalities and back stories. I loved learning about them all separately, and thought it was great when they were finally all thrown together - all of her story subjects meeting one another. It was just a great concept.<br /><br />While Kitty tries to figure out what Constance had in mind for these 100 people, we also find her guilt-wrecked over the school teacher she slandered. There's also the matter of maybe falling in love with her best friend and dealing with her own slander. Her personal and professional lives are in ruins, but as much as she lifts up the lives of the people she's interviewing, they do the same for her. They make her feel better about herself and give her the confidence boost she needs to sell this story to the new and critical chief.<br /><br />There's something magical about Ahern's books. They may be a little cheesy, or a little convenient, or a little this, or a little that, but I'm willing to suspend disbelief for a beautiful story that tugs at my heart-strings like no other author does.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8767459172370355624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2037533580750722734"><b>Journalist Kitty Logan's career is being destroyed by scandal - and now she faces losing the woman who guided and taught her everything she knew. At her terminally ill friend's bedside, Kitty asks - what is the one story she always wanted to write? The answer lies in a file buried in Constance's office: a list of one hundred names. There is no synopsis, nothing to explain what the story is or who these people are. The list is simply a mystery. But before Kitty can talk to her friend, it is too l</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2037533580750722734" style="display:none"><b>Journalist Kitty Logan's career is being destroyed by scandal - and now she faces losing the woman who guided and taught her everything she knew. At her terminally ill friend's bedside, Kitty asks - what is the one story she always wanted to write? The answer lies in a file buried in Constance's office: a list of one hundred names. There is no synopsis, nothing to explain what the story is or who these people are. The list is simply a mystery. But before Kitty can talk to her friend, it is too late. With everything to prove, Kitty is assigned the most important task of her life: to write the story her mentor never had the opportunity to. Kitty not only has to track down and meet the people on the list, but find out what connects them. And, in the process of hearing ordinary people's stories, she starts to understand her own.</b><br /><br />A very poor book from Cecelia Ahern. I usually enjoy her books with their touches of magic but this book was just boring. I raced through it just to get to the end which is probably why I kept losing track of the characters but possibly it's just because I wasn't really gripped by any of them. I was touched by a few parts which is why I've given it two stars, it was very nearly a one-star.</span>

<div id="review_454244135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454244135" />
    <a title="BestChickLit.com" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12115057-bestchicklit-com"><img alt="BestChickLit.com" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396532516p2/12115057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454244135?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BestChickLit.com" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BestChickLit.com" href="/user/show/12115057-bestchicklit-com">BestChickLit.com</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454244135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1079815423179725265">I love Cecelia Ahern’s books, they always have sparkle and a hint of magic – you know it’s not real but it is written in such a way that it feels very possible. This book, however, had no magic or strange unbelievable yet believable elements; which in itself was odd. As a big fan of Ahern’s books I was expecting something more. The story is very clever, an interesting concept and very different from your usual chick lit – I wasn’t disappointed with the book just a bit . . . deflated. This is a w</span>
  <span id="freeText1079815423179725265" style="display:none">I love Cecelia Ahern’s books, they always have sparkle and a hint of magic – you know it’s not real but it is written in such a way that it feels very possible. This book, however, had no magic or strange unbelievable yet believable elements; which in itself was odd. As a big fan of Ahern’s books I was expecting something more. The story is very clever, an interesting concept and very different from your usual chick lit – I wasn’t disappointed with the book just a bit . . . deflated. This is a wonderful story, really thought provoking and poignant, just not a typical Ahern masterpiece.<br /><br />Ahern only tackles a fraction of the names on the list which is a wise move, too many more and it would have been confusing and probably a nightmare to write! Despite my previous moans about this book I couldn’t put it down, it wasn’t a quick read for me as I didn’t want to miss anything and a couple of nights it had me up till 2am. The idea behind this book must have been difficult to tackle and the outcome is a very well written and heart warming story. I really enjoyed this book; I just feel it missed something. Where’s the magic??!!<br /><br />Reviewed by Francesca Verbeeten on behalf of BestChickLit.com</span>

<div id="review_413389365" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413389365" />
    <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books"><img alt="Kayleigh {K-Books}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540157695p2/3996633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413389365?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayleigh {K-Books}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayleigh {K-Books}" href="/user/show/3996633-kayleigh-k-books">Kayleigh {K-Books}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007350469" href="/book/show/15732422-one-hundred-names">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3996633-kayleigh-k-books?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413389365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15141100306785815508"><a href='http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2012/09/early-review-one-hundred-names.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>One Hundred Names Review on K-Books</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"To seek truth is not necessarily to go on a mission all guns blazing in order to reveal a lie, neither is it to be particularly ground-breaking - it is simply to get to the heart of what is real."</i>
</b><br/> <br/>There are no words to explain just how excited I was to receive an ARC of Cecelia Ahern's newest novel, <i>One Hundred Names</i>. Cecelia is without a doubt one of my favourite authors of all time and Cecelia is the reason I am so obsessed with books. I have been a mass</span>
  <span id="freeText15141100306785815508" style="display:none"><a href="http://k-booksxo.blogspot.co.uk/2012/09/early-review-one-hundred-names.html" rel="nofollow noopener">One Hundred Names Review on K-Books</a><br><br><b>
  <i>"To seek truth is not necessarily to go on a mission all guns blazing in order to reveal a lie, neither is it to be particularly ground-breaking - it is simply to get to the heart of what is real."</i>
</b><br> <br>There are no words to explain just how excited I was to receive an ARC of Cecelia Ahern's newest novel, <i>One Hundred Names</i>. Cecelia is without a doubt one of my favourite authors of all time and Cecelia is the reason I am so obsessed with books. I have been a massive fan of Cecelia for years and her first novel, <i>PS I Love You</i>, was the first novel I ever read and loved and was the book that made me fall in love with reading. I was so very excited to start <i>One Hundred Names</i> and as soon as it came through the door I was starting. <i>One Hundred Names</i> is possibly my favourite Cecelia Ahern book as it is just an inspiring beautiful tale and I loved every single moment of it.<br><br>Journalist Kitty made a vital mistake. She didn't check all the facts for a story and now she is public enemy number one. With Kitty's life in tatters all she wants is to hide in her apartment. But when her good friend Constance passes away Kitty is left with the job of writing the story Constance always wanted to write but never got the chance. Left with only an envelope filled with a list of 100 names and nothing else Kitty must embark on a journey to figure out who these people are, what links them? But when learning their stories Kitty just might start to learn her own.<br><br>One think I adore about Cecelia's novels is that every single one of them in uplifting and inspiring. Every single one has such an important message and <i>One Hundred Names</i> is no different. I found <i>One Hundred Names</i> so inspiring, even more so than her previous novels. Everybody makes mistakes and you really can't let those mistakes rule your life. You can't sit dwelling over it forever. Yes mistakes are made every day... you know why? Because we are only human. And all we can do is learn from those mistakes and move on. This is the very important message in <i>One Hundred Names</i> and it's such a beautiful uplifting tale than every single person can relate to.<br><br>Kitty is a great character. I had mixed feelings about her at start. I found her kind of selfish and I didn't particularly like her. She had done this awful thing to somebody and all she could think about was how it impacted her. How it had ruined her life, how she had to deal with the repercussions. Well yes... we made mistakes we have to deal with the consequences and Kitty's mistake was a pretty serious, pretty big mistake to make. But the more I read the more I could feel her growing as a character. She started realising that life is full of mistakes but in order to learn and grow as a person we have to make mistakes in order to learn from them and become a better person. By the end of the book I felt like Kitty was a completely different person. She was kinder and thought about things impacted other people and I loved being on Kitty's journey and seeing the transformation that she goes through.<br><br>Although <i>One Hundred Names</i> is Kitty's journey it is not in any way only Kitty's story. It's many stories wrapped into one and how other people's stories can impact and change yours. I loved seeing all these other characters and how their lives intertwined and changed Kitty for the better. I genuinely loved every moment of this book which to me was no surprise considering Cecelia wrote it. I have not read one book by Cecelia that I haven't loved every moment of it. Her writing is amazing that hooks you right from page one and leaves you breathless by the end of the book.<br><br>Cecelia Ahern's books have no genre... they are in a genre of their own as nothing quite compares to her books. Every single one of them will always be some of my favourite books of all time and they are the books that I will re-read over and over again. Cecelia's books are beautiful and uplifting with a touch of magic added to them. <i>One Hundred Names</i> is a phenomenal book that everyone should read. Such a beautiful, uplifting inspirational journey, this book is not to be missed. A must-read for everyone. Cecelia is such an inspiration and will forever be one of my favourite authors of all time. One Hundred Names left me breathless and I cannot wait till her next novel.<br><br><b>
  <i>"That is what we should be writing about. The unsung heroes, the people who don't believe they are heroes at all because they are just doing what they believe they have to do in their lives."</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1063.photobucket.com/albums/t514/kayleigh-mg/?action=view&amp;current=5-star.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363947i/715472.png" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15141100306785815508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770838465?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurel-Rain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurel-Rain" href="/user/show/1402123-laurel-rain">Laurel-Rain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062248633" href="/book/show/18505788-one-hundred-names">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770838465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1760253857262402659">When Kitty Logan, a journalist, makes a huge mistake in a TV story, the repercussions are numerous. In fact, they are creating ongoing havoc in her life, beginning with a huge lawsuit, the loss of her position on the TV show, and possibly the loss of her job at the magazine Etcetera, created by her mentor Constance.<br/><br/>To add to the pain, her mentor Constance dies. But beforehand, she points Kitty in the direction of a story she wishes she had told. She refers her to a list of names in her files, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText1760253857262402659" style="display:none">When Kitty Logan, a journalist, makes a huge mistake in a TV story, the repercussions are numerous. In fact, they are creating ongoing havoc in her life, beginning with a huge lawsuit, the loss of her position on the TV show, and possibly the loss of her job at the magazine Etcetera, created by her mentor Constance.<br /><br />To add to the pain, her mentor Constance dies. But beforehand, she points Kitty in the direction of a story she wishes she had told. She refers her to a list of names in her files, but has no other instructions for her. Before Kitty can come back with the list for more information, Constance is gone.<br /><br />"One Hundred Names: A Novel" is a story about the truths that lie in the stories behind a random set of ordinary people, each of whom has something extraordinary to share. By putting together the story, Kitty hopes to reclaim her career and redeem herself.<br /><br />Where does Kitty's journey lead her? What life lessons does she glean from the stories of others? And how does her persistence lead to a magical outpouring of love and comfort from her story subjects that will also encompass her with the same feelings?<br /><br />Set in Ireland, taking the reader from Dublin to Cork, the story carried me along, intrigued by Kitty's process of reclaiming her life. Recommended for those who are fans of the author, and for others who love a feel-good story about the magical moments available in everyday life. 4.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1760253857262402659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

From Love, Rosie to this, this book was the perfect mix of light reading encompassing adventure, love and hope. The message at the end was beautiful and I'm not sure if it's just me or the Westlife song "Written in the Stars" I had playing while finishing this, but we all have a story of our own to tell.<br/><br/>..I hope you believe yours is worth telling :) </span>

<div id="review_461898974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461898974" />
    <a title="Suad Shamma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma"><img alt="Suad Shamma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507364224p2/11245979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461898974?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suad Shamma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suad Shamma" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma">Suad Shamma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007350476" href="/book/show/16118673-one-hundred-names">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461898974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16520184726451146222">I love Cecelia Ahern, even when one of her books disappoints, I still cannot get over this authour. She is spectacular in her style of writing, and remembering the impact her first few books had on me is enough for me to remain a loyal fan.<br/><br/>One Hundred Names was a good book, one that kept me reading and intrigued until the very end. However, I cannot bring myself to love this book. The way it was written and the way the story was told and the events unfolded reminded me a little of Emilie Richard</span>
  <span id="freeText16520184726451146222" style="display:none">I love Cecelia Ahern, even when one of her books disappoints, I still cannot get over this authour. She is spectacular in her style of writing, and remembering the impact her first few books had on me is enough for me to remain a loyal fan.<br /><br />One Hundred Names was a good book, one that kept me reading and intrigued until the very end. However, I cannot bring myself to love this book. The way it was written and the way the story was told and the events unfolded reminded me a little of Emilie Richards and Diane Chamberlain's style. Don't get me wrong, Richards and Chamberlain are both great writers too, and I enjoy their books, however that is not what I expect from an Ahern.<br /><br />I expect magic, make believe, enchantment and lots of charm! And that was sorely missing from this book. The concept is quite interesting, Kitty Logan - a journalist - has hit rock bottom when she falsely accused a man on TV and thereby lost her job, her reputation, and credibility as a journalist. Her only living ally is Constance Dubois - but not for long. Constance is suffering from terminal cancer, and is on her deathbed. Before she passes, she tells Kitty that there is one story she wish she'd told. Kitty makes it her mission to tell Constance's story after her death as a sort of tribute to her dear friend and editor, but also as a revival of her own career and life.<br /><br />This story involves a list of one hundred completely random names - and it is up to Kitty to figure out the link between all those names and put it together in a story that makes sense.<br /><br />Interesting, yes. But nothing spectacular about it. I enjoyed meeting the many different characters, the roles they played in Kitty's life, their back stories, the way they developed throughout the book changing their own lives, but also Kitty's. However, I was a little...underwhelmed...by the way it ended. When Kitty finally figured out the link, I expected something out of this world, but it was very ordinary...it lacked luster. Sometimes a little ordinary is good, I'm sure, but like I said, it is not what I expect when reading an Ahern. Furthermore, when Kitty first finds the list of hundred names, I expected a lot more than for her to just get in touch with a fraction of the list (namely 6 people).<br /><br />I read her books for their unrealistic storylines, because Ahern has the gift of making the unrealistic seem attainable, rational even. And she always finds a way of hitting just the right spot in the telling of a story - be it by having an invisible friend, losing things and not knowing where they go, or having none other than Life himself drop by for a visit to give you a reality check. These are the things I love about Ahern, and these are the things I hope she continues to strive for in her stories.<br /><br />This was a good story, but a little too ordinary by Ahern's standards. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16520184726451146222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2347638840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347638840" />
    <a title="Rawa&#39;a" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43449419-rawa-a"><img alt="Rawa&#39;a" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531839527p2/43449419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347638840?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rawa&#39;a" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rawa&#39;a" href="/user/show/43449419-rawa-a">Rawa&#39;a</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43449419-rawa-a?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347638840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16479930349073811628">The last time I read Cecelia Ahern was 2 years ago, after accidentally discovering her through How To Fall In Love on a road trip. I loved it so much that I read 2 more novels written by her. She is for sure a modern fairy tale writer, someone who believes good things are still around - that good people exist and happy endings are real. The teenager me loved that - hope and goodness is a good mix for an aspiring adult; hence, reading her again now did feel good but also carried a feeling of nost</span>
  <span id="freeText16479930349073811628" style="display:none">The last time I read Cecelia Ahern was 2 years ago, after accidentally discovering her through How To Fall In Love on a road trip. I loved it so much that I read 2 more novels written by her. She is for sure a modern fairy tale writer, someone who believes good things are still around - that good people exist and happy endings are real. The teenager me loved that - hope and goodness is a good mix for an aspiring adult; hence, reading her again now did feel good but also carried a feeling of nostalgia for fresh beginnings with many promises and endless possibilities that I then joined in my early years in uni. <br />Additionally, I’m really enjoying reading novels and books written by writers I didn’t read for in a while. It’s interesting to see the contrast between what I thought about them then and never now, along with all the flashbacks in feelings and memories ✨!!<br /><br />Summary: after a drastic turn in her career, Kitty is on a mission to write a story on behalf of her deceased friend. She had a list of 100 names and no other mean into what the story could possibly be out and to find out, she goes on a quest that eventually saved her. <br />The book was good, however, the multiple storylines prevented me from forming the usual strong bond with the main characters. <br /><br />Here are a few quotes:<br />“..a weariness that came from a constant sadness, a hollowness in their hearts. The heart knew that something was missing and it was having to work extra hard to make up for it.”<br /><br />“..but whatever it is, they were just perfectly matched, always the same, always in sync, never seemed separated by anything as large as a decade, apart from the occasional viewpoint. It was as though they had arrived on the planet at the same time and accompanied each other through every day as though they were made to be that way.”<br /><br />“..I woke up and said to myself, I can’t do this. I cannot get through this day. But I did. Somehow. And then that day was over and I was facing the night and I said to myself, I cannot face this night. But I did. Somehow. And then that night was over. I have said the same thing to myself every day and every night since. Each second is rather torturous, as though it will never move on, and as though it will never get any easier, and yet when I look back on it, look where we are. Two weeks on. And I’m doing it. And I still believe I simply cannot.”<br /><br />“I expected the world to end; but it didn’t. Everything kept going, everything is still going. Sometimes I go for walks and I find that I have stopped moving, and everything else is still shifting and evolving all around me. And I wonder, don’t they know? Don’t they know about the terrible thing that has happened?”<br /><br />“You hear about the good ones all the time. Gosh, isn’t so-and-so great, so strong, so brave for doing whatever so soon. I fear I’m not a good widower. I don’t want to do anything. I don’t wish to go anywhere. Most of the time I don’t want to even be here, but you’re not supposed to say that, are you? You’re just supposed to say insightful meaningful<br /> Things that surprise people so that they can tell other people how brave you are. Brave.. but I was never the brave one. Why it should fall upon me to become that now is beyond me.”<br /><br />“I think you should help who you can. I think it will help you.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="16479930349073811628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1909722304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909722304" />
    <a title="Rod Raglin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16616283-rod-raglin"><img alt="Rod Raglin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599717325p2/16616283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909722304?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rod Raglin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rod Raglin" href="/user/show/16616283-rod-raglin">Rod Raglin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909722304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer216256509243709753">Kitty Logan is a disgraced journalist. In her unbridled drive for success she's cut corners and libeled an innocent man. The tabloid television news show she worked for is being sued for a lot of money.<br/><br/>The only one who still believes in Kitty is Constance, an editor and Kitty's mentor, but Constance is dying.<br/><br/>When Kitty asks Constance what story she regrets not writing, Constance tells her to fetch a file folder from her office. In the file is a list of one hundred names and nothing else. Before </span>
  <span id="freeText216256509243709753" style="display:none">Kitty Logan is a disgraced journalist. In her unbridled drive for success she's cut corners and libeled an innocent man. The tabloid television news show she worked for is being sued for a lot of money.<br /><br />The only one who still believes in Kitty is Constance, an editor and Kitty's mentor, but Constance is dying.<br /><br />When Kitty asks Constance what story she regrets not writing, Constance tells her to fetch a file folder from her office. In the file is a list of one hundred names and nothing else. Before Constance can explain the importance of these names or how they're related she dies. <br /><br />Partly because Kitty sees this as an opportunity to salvage her career and partly as a tribute to her late friend she decides to investigate these names and see if she can find and write the story that links them.<br /><br />She can't. Or at least she hadn't been able to forty percent into the novel.<br /><br />Rather than the unfolding of a promising plot premise the reader is presented with Kitty's very ordinary life, with the exception of excrement being smeared on her front door numerous times from irate readers and supporters of the man she libeled.<br /><br />After interviewing a half dozen or so people on Constance' list and getting nowhere Kitty's getting frustrated and so was I.<br /><br />At the beginning I had stretch my suspension of disbelieve to include the improbable plot point the the story hangs on - that a tabloid news show would allow a story to air that accuses a high school teacher of sexual misconduct with a student and fathering her child without solid evidence, like maybe DNA testing. I mean, do they have a death wish?<br /><br />Being a journalist myself I know this would never be allowed to happen. If the reporter was incompetent enough to submit such an incendiary story without irrefutable evidence it would have been killed by the news editor, and for sure never got past the producer.<br /><br />However, besides this grievous lack of research of the author's part I finally abandoned the novel because the story was boring and the writing mediocre.<br /><br />Six names down, ninety-four to go? I don't think so.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="216256509243709753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/15457806-rose">Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13777580660286586304">As I'm typing this, I'm still dizzy after jumping off from the strong-sensations roller-coaster which is the book One Hundred Names, by Cecelia Ahern. It's a positive dizziness, though- overwhelming, actually. At the end of the book, as I reached the "Behind the scenes writing One Hundred Names" pages, I realized that the story had finished and that someone has violently yanked me off this ride full of excitement.<br/>I started reading this book, first of all because of the title, and second, well, t</span>
  <span id="freeText13777580660286586304" style="display:none">As I'm typing this, I'm still dizzy after jumping off from the strong-sensations roller-coaster which is the book One Hundred Names, by Cecelia Ahern. It's a positive dizziness, though- overwhelming, actually. At the end of the book, as I reached the "Behind the scenes writing One Hundred Names" pages, I realized that the story had finished and that someone has violently yanked me off this ride full of excitement.<br />I started reading this book, first of all because of the title, and second, well, the summary is just telling you "Read the book, read the book", so I just had to read it. It was so very intriguing that I just couldn't let it pass by under my nose. I began reading it bit by bit (and by that I mean that I was only taking small bites out of the book- not literally, of course) and then this afternoon, I just went for it and swallowed it whole. There was more than half to read, left, which made it to be about two hundred and fifty pages, or something like that. It was so captivating. <br />Kitty's development in the story is extraordinary. She goes from being unconsciously self-centered, and then, throughout the story, she learns that other people matter, too, and that she isn't the only one struggling. <br />The six "names" that Kitty met in the story, are so love-able and it's it's hard to have to let them go- like you're actually watching them part ways. I never got so easily attached to the characters of a story. <br />"Every table has a story to tell" as the blackboard in the Café said.<br />Five, well-deserved stars for this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13777580660286586304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526542376" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1262067177847884822">Okay, here we go. This review might have minor spoilers. <br/><br/>This book is about Kitty, a reporter who has her reporter career falling apart, her love life even worse and she's struggling with the disease of her friend and "counsellor". <br/>Kitty receive from her a list of 100 names and, without any clue, needs to write a paper for the magazine where she works about all those names. <br/><br/>I was not enjoying this book at the beginning. I'm not sure why. Maybe because I've been reading a lot of books about teena</span>
  <span id="freeText1262067177847884822" style="display:none">Okay, here we go. This review might have minor spoilers. <br /><br />This book is about Kitty, a reporter who has her reporter career falling apart, her love life even worse and she's struggling with the disease of her friend and "counsellor". <br />Kitty receive from her a list of 100 names and, without any clue, needs to write a paper for the magazine where she works about all those names. <br /><br />I was not enjoying this book at the beginning. I'm not sure why. Maybe because I've been reading a lot of books about teenagers lately and suddenly changed to a woman in her thirties with her life all wrecked might have shocked me a little. <br /><br />I also didn't like the translation to Portuguese and the letter type used. I know I seem harsh and rigorous, but my eyes did not adjust to the book for a while and that bothered me. <br /><br />Throughout the story, I really connected with Kitty for one simple reason: she reminds me of myself. I hope I don't have to face all her problems late in life but I can really see myself working on an impossible task because of a friend, or for a friend. I could see myself looking for those people and trying to figure out why they were all in the list. I got really emotional with the ending because it made me wonder if I should be a journalist too and what should I write about if that's my decision. <br /><br />It's a nice book, you can read it quickly. Don't let the beginning slow you down, the ending will make you happy. <br /><br />Xoxo<br />Gabi<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/4317800-penny">Penny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer440771319" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2910161567455314356">The author apparently got the idea for this book upon seeing Jennifer Lawrence on MTV talking about her new movie One Hundred Names. Obviously she had misheard her say The Hunger Games and was so pleased when she found out because she could now steal the title for herself.<br/><br/>About the book though, I started off confused mainly because of the main character Kitty. I went back and forth between liking and hating her and it wasn't until I was three quarters of the way through the book that I decided I</span>
  <span id="freeText2910161567455314356" style="display:none">The author apparently got the idea for this book upon seeing Jennifer Lawrence on MTV talking about her new movie One Hundred Names. Obviously she had misheard her say The Hunger Games and was so pleased when she found out because she could now steal the title for herself.<br /><br />About the book though, I started off confused mainly because of the main character Kitty. I went back and forth between liking and hating her and it wasn't until I was three quarters of the way through the book that I decided I liked her. Kitty is a journalist. When we first meet her she's contrite and regretful because she unknowingly falsely accuses someone on national television of harmful and damaging things. Not too much later we find out she's contrite because of how the backlash affected <i>her</i> life and career, and not the man she falsely accused. This is what confused and annoyed me about her through much of the book, the back and forth of her feelings. She eventually starts researching an article based on a list of one hundred names that was going to be an written by her friend and mentor who passes away suddenly. What I really loved about the book was all the people who made up the list of names. Their stories made me want to keep reading and in turn made Kitty more likable, which I was ultimately glad for.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2910161567455314356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10067197962837230984">Hooray! In the end, I just love this book as I love "How to Fall in Love". The big mistake she had made caused problems not only to the victim but of course herself.   <span id="freeText10067197962837230984" style="display:none">Hooray! In the end, I just love this book as I love "How to Fall in Love". But, this one hook me hard as I dwelve more into the story. <br /><br />We all can relate to Katherine Logan or Kitty Logan. The big mistake she had made caused problems not only to the victim but of course herself. When the world turns their back against you, you'll find yourself struggling to restore their faith, their belief in you especially when you're a reporter. <br /><br />In short, she had to meet 100 people, I mean a total strangers and turned out Kitty's mentor, Constance had never contacted them before which had made it a lot difficult to figure out what Constance had been thinking.<br /><br />It was just impossible to meet 100 people in 2 weeks, wasn't it? Kitty's hardships is simply endearing and that's what helped Kitty into a better person, not the one that believes others' accusation easily. <br /><br />What I get from this book is it makes me realise how we easily outlook people around us. We have reach into one point where we don't care about anyone but ourself. But, we live in a community. That one day will come where we become people in need and you can't help yourself. <br /><br />I just love people more after reading this book </span>

<div id="review_932596101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/932596101" />
    <a title="Jeanette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette"><img alt="Jeanette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372095557p2/11869072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/932596101?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette" href="/user/show/11869072-jeanette">Jeanette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer932596101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5830219515392743824">I'm not being generous, because this novel was much closer to a 3.5 star. But I could not round it up. The reason was because I liked Kitty less and less and less as the book progressed. Honestly- I admired her doggedness in getting to the 5000 words, but really! It was not just because of her loose living either. She seemed to have a density about her to most anything but her own purposes. To me for someone who was basically a writer too? She reacted more than she observed? Not a good friend, n</span>
  <span id="freeText5830219515392743824" style="display:none">I'm not being generous, because this novel was much closer to a 3.5 star. But I could not round it up. The reason was because I liked Kitty less and less and less as the book progressed. Honestly- I admired her doggedness in getting to the 5000 words, but really! It was not just because of her loose living either. She seemed to have a density about her to most anything but her own purposes. To me for someone who was basically a writer too? She reacted more than she observed? Not a good friend, nor very caring (words being quite different than actions). Not even to herself. But the other characterizations of the people on her inherited list were 4 star. And the Dublin setting interesting and new to me in its special flavor. I felt that and enjoyed the story.<br /><br />BTW, I had this on a Kindle library download and read it over 3 days during a driving trip. It was an easy story to drop, return, stop, continue etc. Not all are in that category of such easy continuity. To me that is one mark of a good story teller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5830219515392743824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364923282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4909290326436740241"> Beautiful and inspiring :)<br/><br/>There's so much I want to write about this book, specially about constance, the pursuer of distinct stories and also about Kitty Logan, the fierce, electrified woman who became utterly lost and penitent on account of her own defiance at some point. and then one perplexing list of 100 names written by Constance becomes the turning point of Kitty's life to amend her mistakes and see through life in a different way. <br/> I find it difficult to assemble my thoughts because thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4909290326436740241" style="display:none"> Beautiful and inspiring :)<br /><br />There's so much I want to write about this book, specially about constance, the pursuer of distinct stories and also about Kitty Logan, the fierce, electrified woman who became utterly lost and penitent on account of her own defiance at some point. and then one perplexing list of 100 names written by Constance becomes the turning point of Kitty's life to amend her mistakes and see through life in a different way. <br /> I find it difficult to assemble my thoughts because this book has taught me so much. On the whole about letting go of my own angst and about the importance of second chances. Predominantly about forgiveness and chasing what we crave,doesn't matter how peculiar it gets. <br /><br /><br />I've always been intrigued by Ahern's work and I'll just end my review calling this book the star amongst her novels :) </span>

<div id="review_1034088053" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034088053" />
    <a title="Donna McCaul Thibodeau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34218336-donna-mccaul-thibodeau"><img alt="Donna McCaul Thibodeau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498578289p2/34218336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1034088053?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna McCaul Thibodeau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna McCaul Thibodeau" href="/user/show/34218336-donna-mccaul-thibodeau">Donna McCaul Thibodeau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062248633" href="/book/show/18505788-one-hundred-names">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034088053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4151784539274978262">I really liked the premise of this book. A journalist finds a list of one hundred names and tries to connect the dots to see what links them together. The problem is that the main character in the book is quite unlikeable and as much as I hate to say it, the book itself is just not that well written. I wanted to like it but I'm afraid it's one of those that will be gone from my memory in a week or two.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/6Pq6/Roq71jUzLXZC7paM56F6n9mIlOYRKWdMr0SHuU86w7H+fiS/S5tXHqmcPqhLf1JwqgB6QGf/32OzyWWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4BsZLyCDo1Df1WZuS7wSZ0Ywq8HOsBTVWB1F+AD2X9aLS1//ywzqpkg/4cjFCzjlDP1JTzmImj8/cC568T6B9A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Then one day, her friends and neighbours start to disappear, and she begins to realise that they are not safe after all.\nThrough ten-year-old eyes, Lise tells of her family’s two-year imprisonment in POW camps and the brutal treatment received at the hands of their Japanese captors. For respite from the rat-infested floor of their shelter they adopt a blue door, which sits on concrete posts in the ground. Rav<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2823143626381518976\" style=\"display:none\">This hardback omnibus edition collects three of M. T. Vasudevan Nair’s previously published works—Mist and The Soul of Darkness, Kaalam and Kuttiedathi and Other Stories. The volume features an introduction to M. T. Vasudevan Nair’s work by P. P. Raveendran, an eminent academic and a scholar of Malayalam literature.\n\nMist and The Soul of Darkness are translationsof M. T. Vasudevan Nair’s highly-acclaimed novellas, Manhu and Irutinde Atmavu. In the Mist, set at a hill-station resort, the author narrates the story of Vimala, a school teacher who continues to wait for her beloved Sudhir, with whom she once shared a passionate affair filled with promises. The Soul of Darkness, on the other hand speaks ofVelayudhan, a young man regarded by his family as ‘not normal’ and is thus treated abominably, tortured and beaten. Though his cousin Ammakutty really cares for him, she is helpless and cannot do much to save him. In both stories, Nair voices through mists of memories and emotions, some lost hopes and evocative experiences. The narratives are deeply touching, dramatic and realistic.\n\nSet against the backdrop of a crumbling matrilineal tarawad system of the Nairs in Kerala with its manifold conflicts and problems, Kaalam is the story of Sethumadhavan Nair who starts out as an ambitious and confident adolescent -- but in his journey towards adulthood, where material and social success go hand in hand, he is faced with an overwhelming sense of disillusionment. In its revelations, the story is beautifully adorned with the emotional experiences of the protagonist, which is also reflective of MT’s own childhood in many ways.\n\nKuttiedathi and other stories is a collection of the finest stories of M. T. Vasudevan Nair that encompasses the ordinary middle class lives and sufferings of people in northern Kerala. Nair’s engaging style of storytelling is touching throughout. If the lead story ‘Kuttiedathi’ mixes tragic memory and domestic martyrdom, ‘When the Doors of Heaven Open’ plays out another life upon which centre a group of lives, all selfish, caring and indifferent by turns. In ‘Insight’ however, strange and unfathomable bonds of passion come up as the main theme. These are little tragedies of the soul told with a finesse characteristic of Nair’s profound, yet minimalist sense of expression.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2823143626381518976\" href=\"#\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern">About Cecelia Ahern</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1596427608p3/7116.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern">Cecelia Ahern

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16794167901123307847">Cecelia Ahern was born and grew up in Dublin. She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>
